 Dear Friends!

    Today Myself and shrini have gone to saveetha Engineering college.
First we met Pricipal ,Dean and HOD. They gave warm welcome to us.
After a meet with principal about our activities, we went to seminar hall.
As usual tamil thaai vazhthu and all other formal introductary speechs held.


 I started with the presentation "What/Why opensource?"
I moved the session with more interaction.In that presentation
no where i told "opensource is best".I have just explained the cases,
and asked the question "Which is better?" .

    After my presentation shrini took the "History of Open Source".
He gave the story without any doze to the students by walking among students

and making more interaction.

   After Lunch Mr.Baskar (LinuXperts Systems) gave his presentation.
Then shrini gave the presentation about our ilugc activities.
Due to time constraints  we stopped at 3.15 p.m  and answered the questions.
Finally we wind up with national anthem.

*Lessons learned from this activity:*

1.) We should strictly follow our agenda.

(Due to time constraints we left one more prepared presentation "Jobs in
Opensource" and Installation demo.)

2.) Adoptation with time (Lunch time, tea time...)

3.) What to do ? if power fail... (Power failed for more then 10 times).

4.) If any problem while taking the presentation(Projector problem,power
failure ...), Mean time
we should have some stuff to manage the students.(any interesting story
about opensource or anything)

5.) Colourfull and Interactive presentations gave good results among
students
(Among 45 students, no one slept).

6.) Going with our own laptop is best. (As we dont have own laptop,
we showed the presentations with the college System, which has windoz with
virus ;-).
 As soon as we  inserted our pen drive, It got affected by virus and lost
some files,
changed folder names...etc. Actually we have showed that one as "virus demo"
to the students ;-).

7.) If we have to show the presentations from windoz, we should bring the
presentations in CD.

8.) We should know how to adjust the projector while installation demo.
(Finally we planned to
show the installation demo(Ubuntu Feisty). But, due to frequency problem,
projector didnt render properly.
 So we dropped installation.The projectors are always nightmare to me ;-)).

9.) We should go with PDF viewer, Media Player (VLC...),Open Office and what
ever we
need for our presentation.( We planned to show some videos related to linux,

but due to virus problem we lost the VLC setup file.).


*   Presentation will be uploaded soon....*

Regards,
Bala vignesh

I don't think this is a problem. Nothing can be planned to the last

I think time management is very difficult to get right.

> 3.) What to do ? if power fail... (Power failed for more then 10 times).

> 4.) If any problem while taking the presentation(Projector problem,power
> failure ...), Mean time
> we should have some stuff to manage the students.(any interesting story
> about opensource or anything)

This is something that can surely be done. It is best to ensure that
everything is working hours before the event. In case the premises are
not open by then you have to carry everything with you and ensure that
Murphy's law does not strike. In any case if we take enough pains I
think this can be solved to a large extent.

Planning and anticipating failures is very critical.

> 5.) Colourful and Interactive presentations gave good results among
> students
> (Among 45 students, no one slept).
> 

Yes. Slides are marvelous. Fantastic. In fact I have never seen the idea
of using real life images to convey the practical aspects of open source
working so well.

Your images are superb. Extremely well chosen and so is the layout of
the slides and the text.

I also liked the attribution to flickr and picasa.

I used images from flickr but did not attribute since the photos were in
public domain anyway.

From srini.it at gmail.com  Sat Dec  1 11:18:30 2007
From: srini.it at gmail.com (Srinivasan Sundararajan)
Date: Sat Dec  1 11:18:39 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Presentation at Saveetha Engg College
In-Reply-To: <bc3fff520711301030l16eafe09v9a8d29243d7ac47c@mail.gmail.com>

hi guys, great work. hope I can start imposing on you guys too (apart from
my usual catches of Raman, Bharathi, etc.)

while Raman and others have given valuable comments / suggestions, let me
add a few of my own [a few points may be repeated but with different
flavor].
1. do not worry much about time constraint. with due regard to the FOSS
community -- who want to share all and the latest -- we are addressing the
novices and neoconverts. If 2 of your 4 presentations catch the audience
attention, so much the better.  you can squeeze the other two in a very
minimal time and/or make the offer
    (a) if the audience is willing, another session could be held on a later
date
        [even if you are not available, let us jointly ensure that somebody
goes ]
    (b) if the college cannot host, we can a special session on one of the
saturdays
         at MIT / NRCFOSS or some other college  -- interested students
could come over
        (e.g., Jaya Engg could be developed as the 'norther chennai node')
2. As Raman suggested, ensure that there is a Linux installation demo --
done by a student under your instruction
3. Make an offer that interested students could take up projects -- NRCFOSS
can do the background handholding, talking with the staff , etc., while LUG
members do the mentoring. If needed, the nrcfosshelpline portal can be used
as wiki or code repository. 2nd and 3rd year students will be the prime
targets.
4. each time, take a live cd. in fact, you can leave it with the college so
that 'interested students or staff' could play with it and learn. if you can
catch 2 serious guys/girls from 3 visits, it will be great. [Just as I was
typing this, I got one student from KCG college  -- seems quite serioius --
where I had made a presentation 3 months back!]

please feel free to catch us if we could be of any use.
al the best and continue the good work.
Srinivasan, NRCFOSS

In-Reply-To: <Pine.LNX.4.58.0711190012480.30214@chi.spunge.org>

On Mon, 19 Nov 2007, carti wrote:

> Hi,
> I wanted to see the tamil news sites
>        www.dinamalar.com
>        www.dailythanthi.com
>        www.dinakaran.com
>        thatstamil.oneindia.in
>
> I used Internet Explorer 6. After I downloaded the fonts everything(all
> the sites) worked fine(shown properly in nicely readable format).
>
> The same thing when I tried with Firefox 2.0.0.9, it is not showing the
> sites properly.
>
> I use Windows XP home edition(Though I use Linux out of my interest), I
> need to used windows xp for unavoidable circumstances. So, NO Flame wars
> or advises to go to Linux. ;)
>
> I searched in net; though pointed to various sites, nothing were much
> useful. I dont want to use scripts(like greasemonkey kind of stuffs).
>
> When things work so well with Internet Explorer, IS it so difficult for
> Firefox to work properly.
>
> Note: Same question I posted long time before but did not get any fruitful

> and figured out a solution, so, I am asking again.

> _______________________________________________

Hi All,

Though, this is related to the MS-Windows XP and Firefox, this might help
people who are trying to find the solution.
I got several responses from different people for the Problem related to
Tamil in Firefox(In Windows). To be frank, nothing worked.

I saw the solution from a web site(forum). Thank you very much for the
person whoever has posted that. Here is the link of that.

http://www.themediasite.net/forums/showthread.php?t=30899

Here is the solution mentioned there.

=============================
     Control Panel -> Regional and Language Options -> Languages Tab ->
Enable "Install files for complex script and right-to-left languages(including
Thai)".

     You need to put the installation CD.

     After intallation, reboot the PC.

     Upon, starting the machine and Firefox, it worked perfectly fine.
=============================

From shakthimaan at gmail.com  Sat Dec  1 15:04:19 2007
From: shakthimaan at gmail.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Sat Dec  1 15:04:31 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Presentation at Saveetha Engg College
In-Reply-To: <bc3fff520711301030l16eafe09v9a8d29243d7ac47c@mail.gmail.com>
References: <bc3fff520711301030l16eafe09v9a8d29243d7ac47c@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <d16b1c80712010134t4a9f28d1r7b685ded130c8bcc@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

----- On Dec 1, 2007 12:00 AM, BalaVignesh Kasinathan
<kbalavignesh@gmail.com> wrote:
| *Lessons learned from this activity:*
|
| 1.) We should strictly follow our agenda.
\--

It is ok if you don't follow the agenda. The audience might want to
hear something new, and it is ok to address that. But, you should
always follow time constraints. If you have many speakers, and there
is delay then it might not give other speakers' a chance to address
the audience.

-----
| 3.) What to do ? if power fail... (Power failed for more then 10 times).
\--

Prior to any workshop ask for a whiteboard and whiteboard markers, and
if power fails, start doing:

1. Brainstorming sessions.
2. Teach them concepts.     ... (1)

Make sure you don't use permanent markers :)

-----
| (Projector problem,power
| failure ...), Mean time
| we should have some stuff to manage the students.(any interesting story
| about opensource or anything)
\--

See (1) above.

-----
| 6.) Going with our own laptop is best.
\--

Yes, if you have one. If you have it, you should go atleast one hour
before the start of the workshop, so you can test your laptop with the
projector. If it doesn't work you have atleast an hour to find
alternatives:

1. School/college PC with a liveCD
2. Install any distro on a school/college PC and use it.

-----
| 7.) If we have to show the presentations from windoz, we should bring the
| presentations in CD.
\--

Even otherwise, every speaker who comes to the workshop, must have a
copy of all the presentations, code examples etc. of all the other
speakers.

Keep one copy online before the workshop, in case, you want to
download them from the Internet from the school/college labs.

Thumb drives are not expensive these days.

-----
| 9.) We should go with PDF viewer, Media Player (VLC...),Open Office and what
| ever we
| need for our presentation.
\--

If possible, keep presentation slides in many formats (.odp, .pdf,
.html etc.), so you give the user the choice to view the presentation
in whichever format they want (and not impose proprietary formats like
.ppt on the end user).

SK

-- 
Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

I have a solution to these problems. use any pendrive linux.

Solutions:

6th point with pendrive linux:

directly booting with your pendrive make your system go to linux not to
windows. So no virus at all.

7th and 9th point with pendrive linux:

All your linux ready softwares will be present on your pendrive linux. so no
need to bother about installing openoffice, VLC media player. nowadays,
pendrive linux distros have the ability to save changes. So updating your
contents is also possible.

I personally feel puppylinux is better to fit this situation. because I am
using puppy in somewhat relative situation like urs, that is 'a browsing
center linux user'.

My script 
/sbin/iptables -t nat -A PREROUTING -p tcp -d 59.x.x.x
--dport 25 -j DNAT --to-destination 192.168.x.x
/sbin/iptables -t nat -A PREROUTING -p tcp -d 59.x.x.x
--dport 110 -j DNAT --to-destination 192.168.x.x

On Monday 03 Dec 2007, kannan krishnamurthy wrote:

> My name is Kannan. In my office we have installed
> Redhat E.S 4.0 for mail server and Redhat 9.0 for
> Gateway server.

Any particular reason for sticking with RH9.0 and a Gateway server?  
IIRC, there is no support for it i.e. security updates etc.

> when ever my branch office try to send mails to other
> domains it immediately bounce back with an error
> message " The message could not be sent because one of
> the recipients was rejected by the server. The
> rejected e-mail address was ?kannan_6074@yahoo.com?.
> Subject ?test? Account: ?Lawindia?, Server
> ?59.144.x.x?, Protocol:SMTP, Server Response: ?554
> kannan_6074@yahoo.com: Relay access denied?, Port: 25,
> Secure [SSL]: No, Server Error: 554, Error Number:
> 0x800CCC79."

You have to configure your MTA to allow relay to other domains.  The 
error message above clearly states so.  I would strongly suggest SMTP 
AUTH in order to accept messages for relaying.  Postfix has excellent 
docs at www.postfix.org and other forums.

-- Arun Khan

From akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in  Tue Dec  4 20:46:48 2007
From: akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in (Kumar Appaiah)
Date: Tue Dec  4 20:39:38 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] creating sudo user
In-Reply-To: <13286728.1196773039626.JavaMail.root@127.0.0.1>
References: <13286728.1196773039626.JavaMail.root@127.0.0.1>
Message-ID: <20071204151648.GA8101@debian.akumar.iitm.ac.in>

On Tue, Dec 04, 2007 at 06:27:19PM +0530, Mahalingam Subramaniam wrote:
> Hi
> could anyone help in describing the steps involved in creating sudo user on server with all prviliges like root user?
> Thanks in advance

Type visudo, and add the following line:

myuser         ALL = (ALL) ALL

Then myuser has all the privileges as root, and sudo -s will give
him/her a root shell.

HTH.

Kumar

From akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in  Tue Dec  4 21:06:58 2007
From: akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in (Kumar Appaiah)
Date: Tue Dec  4 21:07:09 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] creating sudo user
In-Reply-To: <e597802d0712040727l3756361dleb101862e5392793@mail.gmail.com>
References: <13286728.1196773039626.JavaMail.root@127.0.0.1>

	<e597802d0712040727l3756361dleb101862e5392793@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <a0c4f6270712040736u7fffd5dbk35eca0ed7ec95fe5@mail.gmail.com>

On 04/12/2007, Krishna P wrote:
> On Dec 4, 2007 4:16 PM, Kumar Appaiah wrote:
> > Type visudo, and add the following line:
> >
> or Type vi /etc/sudoers and the rest are same

I disagree. visudo is the right way because (I quote from the visudo man page):

"visudo edits the sudoers file in a safe fashion, analogous to
vipw(8).  visudo locks the sudoers file against multiple simultaneous
edits, provides basic sanity checks, and checks for parse errors.  If
the sudoers file is currently being edited you will receive a message
to try again later."

So, if it's a multiadmin server, say, this is always safer.

HTH.

Kumar

Kumar Appaiah,

Indian Institute of Technology Madras,
Chennai - 600036

On 18:27:19 Dec 04, Mahalingam Subramaniam wrote:
> Hi
> could anyone help in describing the steps involved in creating sudo user on server with all prviliges like root user?
> Thanks in advance

What is your real goal?

sudo is used for allowing select users to run select commands. It is
required for tightening security and avoiding giving root privilege to
users at all costs.

You can learn a lot about it in the man pages and of course google.

If you tell us for what purpose you need to give sudo access then
someone could guide you thro' the process in case you get stuck.

linux man pages are hard to read in the beginning but as time passes by
you will get comfortable with it.

Best of luck !

-Girish

sugar, or black coffee, or coffee with bun. You can have tea with

From gopal at gopalarathnam.com  Wed Dec  5 08:17:50 2007
From: gopal at gopalarathnam.com (Gopal Venkatesan)
Date: Wed Dec  5 08:20:33 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Regarding: How to use PHP with PERL
In-Reply-To: <aefff4620712041324x531d6387oa76c2026662e1e08@mail.gmail.com>
References: <aefff4620712041324x531d6387oa76c2026662e1e08@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20071205024750.GA18889@althoughleave-dr.bangalore.corp.yahoo.com>

On Wed, Dec 05, 2007 at 02:54:59AM +0530, kumaran partanthaman wrote:
> Greeting Friends,
> 
> How to use PHP with PERL, can anybody idea about this please guide to me. I
> am working as programmer in PHP. I plan to study in perl. Please anybody
> give some idea about perl and interact with php.
> 

Greetings.

If your question is how to exchange data between PHP and Perl, the
simplest form of data exchange (that can be parsed easily) is
JSON[1].  Both the languages have their own extensions to parse JSON
format and they're very fast[2].

If you want to learn about JSON, you can grab my presentation from
here[3].

I guess that answers your question.

[1] http://json.org/
[2] Don't use the PEAR JSON package for PHP, there is one in PECL that
    is written in C, its very performant.
[3] http://gopalarathnam.com/talks/JSON_FOSSin2006.pdf

-- 
Gopal Venkatesan

http://gopalarathnam.com/weblog/

> domains it immediately bounce back with an error

> the recipients was rejected by the server. The
> rejected e-mail address was ?kannan_6074@yahoo.com?.
> Subject ?test? Account: ?Lawindia?, Server
> ?59.144.x.x?, Protocol:SMTP, Server Response: ?554
> kannan_6074@yahoo.com: Relay access denied?, Port: 25,
> Secure [SSL]: No, Server Error: 554, Error Number:
> 0x800CCC79."
> 

Seems to be a case of missing relay entry in the access table.

try this,

edit /etc/mail/access to add

yourbranchserip		RELAY


than,


# cd /etc/mail
# makemap hash access.db <  access


- Kiran

ILUGC Meet (Dec 08th):-
=====================

Time : Sat Dec 08th 15:00 IST 2007
Venue: ADI-TeNeT Seminar Hall,
       #CSD 320, ESB, IIT-Madras.

Map: http://chennailug.org/tenet

Agenda:

> Talk: jQuery - The Write Less, Do More (1:30Hrs)
  By Girish Venkatachalam

Abstract:

This will be a short informal intro about the Web Application
toolkit by name jQuery. The main focus will be  basics of web
development. How the different components viz., HTML, CSS, DOM,
JavaScript and AJAX work together to bring a desktop experience
to the Web will be discussed.

Highlights of the talk include:

- Syntax, Semantics and jQuery philosophy
- Simple Web Animations with jQuery
- How AJAX programming is simplified with jQuery
- Rich plug-in support for most common UI needs

Speaker is a regular author in the Linux Journal. Currently he is 
focusing on kick-starting a start-up in Chennai.

Link: http://jquery.com/

* Distribution of Mandriva 2008 Live CDs and Strikers
* Discussion about FossConf Chennai Feb08

HTH :)

Bharathi S

From shriramadhas at gmail.com  Wed Dec  5 20:25:38 2007
From: shriramadhas at gmail.com (=?utf-8?b?4K644K+N4K6w4K+A4K6w4K6+4K6u4K6k4K6+4K644K+N?=)
Date: Wed Dec  5 20:26:25 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Beyond boundaries..
Message-ID: <200712052025.38994.shriramadhas@gmail.com>

Was at a FOSS introduction workshop held at Sammanthurai, 360 KM to the South 
of Colombo, the capital city of Sri Lanka (Dec 01 and 02).

First travel abroad. NRCFOSS, Ubuntu Community, South Eastern University of 
Sri Lanka, Sri Lanka LUG share the credits for this event.

On Dec 01, after a hectic travel of little less than ten hours from Colombo, 
we reached Sammanthurai crossing the hill town Kandi (If you are a Cricket 
fan you should be aware, its here Muralitharan broke Shane Warne?s record few 
days back).

Mauran of our team had made prior arrangements for the event. The event 
started with all formalities there, we had with us Hon. Metha Vihari 
(Buddhist Monk) who addressed the students to begin with.

Later to a question asked to him as to why he chose to use free software, he 
told the gathering, since he is a Monk, he cannot afford to pay ?too? much 
for the software he may use.

Also since he is a Monk he can not say ?NO? to some one who asks for a copy of 
the software. Since sharing is one of the foremost of all prerequisites of a 
Monk. To say that I can?t share is simply un-ethical.

few snaps at: http://amachu.net/kadambam/main.php?g2_itemId=89&g2_page=2

to be continued...

Sri Ramadoss M

From akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in  Thu Dec  6 09:56:22 2007
From: akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in (Kumar Appaiah)
Date: Thu Dec  6 09:49:08 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Sourcecode for commands in linux with Documentation
In-Reply-To: <9328ba920712052010y5a628079t60176703b7dbb6fb@mail.gmail.com>
References: <9328ba920712050114s297b270ey97fcf0d426a715cb@mail.gmail.com>
	<dd680c2b0712051002j70ba3cd7pf075f60aff743c60@mail.gmail.com>
	<9328ba920712052010y5a628079t60176703b7dbb6fb@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20071206042621.GA13282@debian.akumar.iitm.ac.in>

On Thu, Dec 06, 2007 at 09:40:50AM +0530, santhosh kumar wrote:
> i need surcecode for "top" command;
> is their any way to get the sourcecode with documentation;
> but man command gives me only the parameter discriptions sir;
> but i need sourcecode discription sir;
> please give me stepwise solution to get the source code;
> please help me to get it.........

If you are using Debian or Ubuntu, then the best way is to find out
which package the file is in and get the source using apt-get
(assuming you have deb-src entries in sources.list).

[kumar@debian ~/Debian/DPMT/enthought-kiva/trunk] apt-file search /usr/bin/top
libwww-topica-perl: usr/bin/topica2mail
procps: usr/bin/top
tcpquota: usr/bin/topmasq
tcpquota: usr/bin/topnet
tcpquota: usr/bin/toptcp

OK, so wee need procps.

[kumar@debian /tmp] apt-get source procps

Hi Guys,
   I'm looking for some smart kids who can work during weekends, 
evenings etc from home.

Requirements:
1)1st or 2nd or 3rd year BE/B.Tech student in a college (no final year 
students or  M.Techs)
2)Very good in Mathematics. 
3)Little experience with programming - any language .
4)Familiar with  linux system -  basic commands like ls.
5)You should have access to some computer.
6)Expert in searching Google, getting things done without much help.
7)Passion for programming or Maths or both.



What will you do with us?
1)JavaScript, PHP programming (60 %)
2)Linux / Apache admin (10 %)
3)A bit of boring work - browse, gather information, and present it in 
nice PDF format. (30%)


How to apply?
1) Do not send your resume.
2) Did you take IIT Mains ? what is your All India Rank ?  (If you are 
an undergraduate in IIT, then you are almost in)
3) Do you have a blog ? or a webpage ? 
4) What is your IRC nick ?  Do you participate in any mailing lists ? If 
so give me the urls that contain your threads.
5) Do you have a pet project ?  ( can be one of those that you did in 
12th std for board exams .. but it should be your *own* idea)
6) Which college do you study ? What course ?  What are your plans  for 
final semester project ?  (your own ideas only)
7) Best time to call you on Skype. After 0700 PM, Indian time.


I'm looking only for one student. The selected one will directly work 
with me and some of my friends in Bangalore. You can take off during 
exams. You only need to work 10 days in a month. I will pay 2k for every 
day you work and hence 20k/month.  *I am not responsible for your 
grades. Your grades will go down once you start working for me.*  I will 
also pay for a good broadband connection.  Before you start working I 
will pay you 2k advance ( assuming you qualify the interview).   I will 
coach you on PHP, JS, CSS, Linux etc. We will communicate via email, IM, 
Skype. We will also use http://www.assembla.com/ - a tool to manage 
agile  development teams spread over.

-- 
Deepan

ILUGC Meet (Dec 08th):-
=====================

Time : Sat Dec 08th 15:00 IST 2007
Venue: ADI-TeNeT Seminar Hall,
       #CSD 320, ESB, IIT-Madras.

Map: http://chennailug.org/tenet

Agenda:

> Talk: jQuery - Write Less, Do More (1:30Hrs)
  By Girish Venkatachalam

Abstract:

This will be a short informal intro about the jQuery, Web Application
toolkit. The main focus will be basics of web development. How the
different components viz., HTML, CSS, DOM, JavaScript and AJAX work
together to bring a desktop experience to the Web will be discussed.

Highlights of the talk include:

- Syntax, Semantics and jQuery philosophy
- Simple Web Animations with jQuery
- How AJAX programming is simplified with jQuery
- Rich plug-in support for most common UI needs

Speaker is a regular author in the Linux Journal. Currently he is
focusing on kick-starting a start-up in Chennai.

Link  : http://jquery.com/
Slides: http://sirsasana.org/jquery.pdf

* Distribution of Free Mandriva 2008 Live CDs & Strikers
* Discussion about FossConf Chennai Feb08

From girishvenkatachalam at gmail.com  Fri Dec  7 14:55:04 2007
From: girishvenkatachalam at gmail.com (Girish Venkatachalam)
Date: Fri Dec  7 14:55:21 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT] karaoke software sug
In-Reply-To: <9abe59030712070004y3f193dd6n8cb82cd5f07252d9@mail.gmail.com>
References: <9abe59030712070004y3f193dd6n8cb82cd5f07252d9@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20071207092504.GA19951@saraswathy.susmita.org>

On 13:34:50 Dec 07, sam sharma wrote:
> hi,
> I have searching the net for sofhtware which can extract the music
> alone(minus 1 track) from a audio file(cda or mp3) for a school function.
> but i could find any things.
> Can you suggest some names for the software which can fit my needs.

It is hard to get it right but mplayer can do it.

For the complete story  check out 

http://linuxjournal.com/9815

And to cut a long story short,

$ mplayer -ao pcm:file=novoice.wav -af karaoke song.mp3

I tried it with some Illayaraja songs, my ever favorite music director
and it worked very well with some. 

You should realize that this is a theoretically intractable problem to
solve given the fact that once mixed you cannot remove.

However it the tracks are stored separately it is trivial.

There are plenty of tools for audio processing in linux.

I know sox and audacity.

Then there is hydrogen, rosegarden and so on.

Check out Dave Phillip's blog in linuxjournal.

He writes  brilliant articles about audio on linux.

He is one of the best authors of LJ and a very impressive musician
himself.

-Girish

PS: I think Gautami owes me a treat for popularizing her in the West

Had the same problem and got the same errors as well. Mostly its a
faulty RAM, but then again run a full scan using smartmontools to see if
its your hard disk. But in my case atleast, It was a screwy RAM. You can
also run memtest to check for errors in RAM

From sudhir at openlx.com  Mon Dec 10 01:36:20 2007
From: sudhir at openlx.com (Sudhir Gandotra)
Date: Mon Dec 10 01:35:40 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] (long mail - a report) Linux & FOSS workshop at Acharya
	Narendra Dev College (Delhi University) & formation of College LUG
Message-ID: <1197230780.5670.92.camel@laptop.censusindia.net>

                         LINUX & FOSS WORKSHOP

 ORGANIZED BY : ACHARYA NARENDRA DEV COLLEGE, jointly with OPENLX LINUX

      Venue : Acharya Narendra Dev College, Govindpuri, New Delhi.

          Date : 6 & 7 December 2007. Time : 0930 to 1730 hrs.


Initially planned as a simple Linux familiarization workshop for staff
and students of the college, it became as a full-fledged LINUX & FOSS
WORKSHOP with speakers and visitors from outside the college and Media,
apart from the college students and faculty.


The workshop was organized by the college jointly with OpenLX Linux who
brought in the expert speakers, its own team and expertise to build a
futuristic event.


Dr. Savithri Singh, Principal, Acharya Narendra Dev College, welcomed
Prof. Poonam Bedi (Head, Department of Computer Science, University of
Delhi), the speakers and the participants to the workshop. In her
remarks she explained how she was introduced to Linux and Wikipidia and
her initial interesting experience with Linux. She wondered if
Universities across the world can use Linux for education, why can't we
in India do it. She mentioned that this workshop is aimed to become an
example and that we should take the torch of Linux knowledge to all the
other colleges of Delhi University, creating a live example for all. She
explained how various Governments across the world including the Kerala
State Government have declared ?NO? to windows and ?YES? to exclusive
usage of Linux for their work. ?There is a gradual realization and shift
towards Linux across the globe?, she said. Delhi University has taken
the first step by giving us the new computers with Linux installed and
now we are taking it forward in our college. One of the college lab is
now 100% Linux, and another one is dual boot. Now, we all will learn and
master Linux and move ahead. We are committed for Linux, she declared.
She explained the importance of the availability of source code and how
this helps students learn the technology, and that, this is not possible
on windows, it being a closed source proprietory technology. She
announced that there will be more such workshop for more people and
follow-up workshops for current participants on advanced subjects of
Linux, to expand and enhance the learning. She declared that personally
as well as college Principal, she is fully committed to Linux. She
invited the participants to learn the maximum and take it to others
around them, thus spreading real-education. 


The workshop was formally Inaugurated by Prof. Poonam Bedi (Head,
Department of Computer Science, University of Delhi), who extended her
full support to this trend-creating event and wished that such
activities happen across the University in all the colleges. She
explained the Linux initiative at Delhi University and the support that
Linux implementations and usage has started receiving from various
quarters. 


Comparing between Linux, Windows and Macintosh, she explained the
advantages of Linux vis-a-vis the other two and urged the audience to
try Linux, it being Free, Open Source and Virus-free. She thanked the
audience for participating in the event and wished a great success to
the event.

Sudhir Gandotra, C.E.O. OpenLX Linux introduced Linux explaining the
Freedom, Open Source etc. aspects of it. Using a slide show he explained
to participants the reasons why Linux is the only choice for true
education in I.T. And urged the authorities to convert the syllabus from
being product-oriented to technology oriented.

Connecting Linux machine to Internet through data-card (without needing
any driver to use the data-card), it was demonstrated to the
participants (through www.netcraft.com website) that even microsoft was
running their server (download.microsoft.com) using Linux as the OS.
Participants wondered if this was the case of that builder who would not
live in building made by himself. !


During the practical session, the participants were given a Linux
installed computer to use it the way they wished. In this session, there
was no agenda and it was found that participants started exploring
various applications/tools on the KDE that was available to them on
these machines having OpenLX Linux installed there.

While they all started working as ROOT user, they were explained the
security risk attached and were shown how to create a user and they all
shifted from ROOT user to GUEST user.


Post lunch, there was a demonstration on how to do RAD programming using
QT, by Ratheesh from OpenLX.

Next was the 12th standard student Arjun Asthana who explained the C++
programming on Linux. Explaining that Turbo C was based on standards of
1993, he urged the authorities to move ahead so that college students
can learn Programming on latest standards.

Later in the practical session, he also explained how it was possible to
run Turbo C in Linux using DosBox so that Linux machines can be used to
study this compulsory topic till the authorities decide to modernize the
curriculum.

Arjun, being so young and having over 6 years' experience of programming
on Linux became a hit among the participants who all wanted to ask him
so many things. In his simple unassuming style, Arjun was seen answering
all their questions, many times talking about the standards, the
technologies being used on Linux and the advanced possibilities that
existed for students on Linux.

We hope his example will inspire the participants to move strongly
towards exploring Linux and finding a new future that awaits them all.


Day Two :

Thanks to Rajiv Chopra, Editor, Linux for You, Atanu Datta (Editorial
Coordinator) was with us to share his experience as a User and gave very
simple-straight forward and inspiring response to the problems
(imaginary) of many users who by now were planning to migrate to Linux.
This was an interesting session, where, many times, we saw the imaginary
aspects being responded by real life experience.

The important of actually using Linux was seen and the participants
agreed that their practical exposure of first day had shown them that
everything looked very much similar. To that extent, they had no fear of
getting into an unknown zone and were already interested in migrating to
Linux.

Some users had already called the OpenLX team last evening taking tips
on installing it on their home computers and some had brought their
computers to college to have OpenLX Linux installed.


A complete demonstration of dual-boot installation was given, resulting
in all of them agreeing to do it on their computers over the weekend.

The Linux DVDs were made available to participants at very special
affordable prices.


Mr. S. K. Goel, Vice President (I.T.), Om Logistics along with his team
from the company, explained how their company became a 100% Linux user,
resulting in ZERO-Downtime and no errors, bringing in not only huge
savings but also the best possible security and stability to their
operations.

He emphasized that even if Linux had cost them many times more, they
would have chosen it, as this level of security-stability and virus-free
situation was not even imaginable on windows.

He also informed of a survey in their company wherein employees did not
want even a raise for using windows, as their productivity had increased
many times by using Linux.


The demonstration of KOHA Library software was given as another live
example of how an Open Source project and surpassed the standards set by
the world and now KOHA is setting the global standards for Library
software.


Dr. Savithri Singh, in her closing remarks, thanked the participants and
OpenLX on making the show a complete success and re-iterated her
commitment to Linux and invited participants to take this forward
strongly.

She hoped that the need of anti-virus software in her college would stop
now that everyone would happily shift to Linux.


Intex Computers demonstrated their ?OpenLX-Linux pre-installed? Desktops
and Laptops, making people aware that such computers are now readily
available in the market, giving people the choice of buying Linux
?pre-installed and bundled? computers, and saving the cost of windows
when they don't want it.


ANDC LUG (Linux Users Group) was formed and all participants happily
became its members. The LUG will have its mailing list formed
immediately and start having its regular meeting. Sudhir Gandotra
explained them the functioning of LUGs and how they can interact with
other LUGs and experts and grow forward on the Linux path of freedom.


A Clustering Lab will be setup at college with the help of OpenLX Linux.
College students will participate in building future versions of OpenLX
Linux by working on its source code at the college lab.

Pictures (some of them) & report are at : www.openlx.com/andc/index.html



        Peace, Force & Joy!   Sudhir Gandotra.  98-101-20918

1/G, Shrikrishna Sansthan Building, Bistupur, Jamshedpur 831001, India

http://registration.fossconf.in/code/wiki/TuotorialSessions

2. About 15 talks are registered so far.

3. About 40 people registered as delegates
    (http://registration.fossconf.in/web/)

Sponsorship

        The approximate cost of the event will be about
	Rs.5 lakhs. It is planned to approach software
	companies and others for sponsorship. They 
	will get publicity proportionate to amount, in
	the form of banners, logos in website etc.
	The required documentation like receipts will
	be from NRCFOSS.
	
	We are planning to fix the minimum amount as
	Rs.5000/-. Offcourse no decision taken yet.


What Luggies can do
	a.Volunteer to take the session in Track 1 and Track 2.
           Please register in the wiki itself.

	b.Volunteers to take care of the stalls, training and 
          supporting student volunteers.

	c.Volunteer to be part of the organising team.

	d.Make Presentations on topic of  choice in Track -3.

	e.Sponsor or find sponsors.

        f.Advertise among friends,collegues and others about
           the event.

From amartyo at gmail.com  Wed Dec 12 09:41:20 2007
From: amartyo at gmail.com (amartyo banerjee)
Date: Wed Dec 12 09:41:31 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Subversion server compromised (again).
Message-ID: <3b15edbe0712112011l2486f580w837477571d2c7622@mail.gmail.com>

Hello everyone,

I had posted previously to the list about a subversion server at work
that I thought was compromised.
See http://article.gmane.org/gmane.org.user-groups.linux.ilugc/39820/

After I got confirmation of that the suggested steps were followed,
i.e. rebuild the box, reinstall, and take certain security measures to
prevent a repeat of events. All external access was removed, so the
box was only accessible from the internal lan. Only 2 net services
were running on the box, ssh and subversion using apache. Root logins
using ssh was disabled, and also password based ssh logins. It was set
up so that ssh could only be accessed using RSA/DSA keys. As before, I
am not the admin for that box or in general. I am the designated
person for creating new repositories or adding subversion users, that
is all. Inspite of that, it was me who implemented the security
measures listed above.

While I was away on vacation my boss called me to say the root
password on the box had been changed again, and he asked if I had
changed it. I had not, which means the box is compromised again. This
time the intruder took steps to cover his tracks. The .bash_history
file of root was not deleted, but there were no entries after a
certain point. The same was the case with /var/log/secure*, there were
no entries after a certain point, but the files existed and were not
zero sized. Nor was there any unusual accounts visible in /etc/passwd
or /etc/shadow with a user id of 0. Therefore it was not possible to
figure out what the intruder did after getting in or how he got in at
all.

Figuring out what happened is beyond my skills or that of anyone here,
and I have no training in this area anyway. Whatever I did last time
was based on reading some old Linux Journal articles. Obviously the
box has to be flattened and rebuilt, but it is important to find out
how it was compromised so we can plug those holes, whether in the
firewall settings, the general lan configuration and the software
running on the box.

I did some reading up on rootkits and learnt about user-level and
kernel-level rootkits, and it may be that something like that has been
installed. This may be another reason I can't figure out what
happened. From what I've read about rootkits, they are nearly
impossible to detect, can be setup to persist even after a reboot and
if the rootkit is a kernel module, it can attach itself to another
module, and so on. Like I said, it is beyond my ability to figure out
if there is any rootkit installed. I am also afraid of inadvertently
destroying evidence in my ignorance, if I do try to find out.

Anyway, I finally come to my questions. Does anybody have any
suggestions where one get hold of a computer forensics and/or security
professional? They would have to have a high enough level of knowledge
to figure out how the intruder got in, what he/she did on the box,
given that the usual evidence has been wiped. It might be that the
intruder still managed to leave some traces, and I hope to find
someone knowledgeable and experienced enough to discover those traces.
Also, they would need to be able to figure out if the intruder came in
from another compromised machine on the lan, and how many boxes on the
lan have been compromised, whether from the subversion server or
otherwise. The lan consists of mostly windows machines, and a few
linux boxes and a few macs. I fear that every machine on the lan has
been compromised too, either from the subversion box this time, or
perhaps from last time, or some other way.

If anybody has dealt with forensics people, could they share their
experiences? Like which professional / firm did a good job and which
ones to avoid.

Subject: [Ilugc] Subversion server compromised (again).
In-Reply-To: <3b15edbe0712112011l2486f580w837477571d2c7622@mail.gmail.com>
References: <3b15edbe0712112011l2486f580w837477571d2c7622@mail.gmail.com>

Hi Amartyo

Is there anyone apart from root who has root privileges . The very same
issue i too had when my servers root password got changed twice which was
running on a redhat 9 machine . I installed rootkit hunter but it did not
show anything. Before i started handeling the server there were some people
who had root access ( the uid field in the /etc/passwd field had been set to
0 ). Then one day a senior with root access came to me and said that he is
not able to change his password. He used to type passwd command to change
his password and as a result changed the root password. I wonder if same is
the case with you.

On Dec 12, 2007 9:41 AM, amartyo banerjee <amartyo@gmail.com> wrote:

> Hello everyone,
>
> I had posted previously to the list about a subversion server at work
> that I thought was compromised.
> See http://article.gmane.org/gmane.org.user-groups.linux.ilugc/39820/
>
> After I got confirmation of that the suggested steps were followed,
> i.e. rebuild the box, reinstall, and take certain security measures to
> prevent a repeat of events. All external access was removed, so the
> box was only accessible from the internal lan. Only 2 net services
> were running on the box, ssh and subversion using apache. Root logins
> using ssh was disabled, and also password based ssh logins. It was set
> up so that ssh could only be accessed using RSA/DSA keys. As before, I
> am not the admin for that box or in general. I am the designated
> person for creating new repositories or adding subversion users, that
> is all. Inspite of that, it was me who implemented the security
> measures listed above.
>
> While I was away on vacation my boss called me to say the root
> password on the box had been changed again, and he asked if I had
> changed it. I had not, which means the box is compromised again. This
> time the intruder took steps to cover his tracks. The .bash_history
> file of root was not deleted, but there were no entries after a
> certain point. The same was the case with /var/log/secure*, there were
> no entries after a certain point, but the files existed and were not
> zero sized. Nor was there any unusual accounts visible in /etc/passwd
> or /etc/shadow with a user id of 0. Therefore it was not possible to
> figure out what the intruder did after getting in or how he got in at
> all.
>
> Figuring out what happened is beyond my skills or that of anyone here,
> and I have no training in this area anyway. Whatever I did last time
> was based on reading some old Linux Journal articles. Obviously the
> box has to be flattened and rebuilt, but it is important to find out
> how it was compromised so we can plug those holes, whether in the
> firewall settings, the general lan configuration and the software
> running on the box.
>
> I did some reading up on rootkits and learnt about user-level and
> kernel-level rootkits, and it may be that something like that has been
> installed. This may be another reason I can't figure out what
> happened. From what I've read about rootkits, they are nearly
> impossible to detect, can be setup to persist even after a reboot and
> if the rootkit is a kernel module, it can attach itself to another
> module, and so on. Like I said, it is beyond my ability to figure out
> if there is any rootkit installed. I am also afraid of inadvertently
> destroying evidence in my ignorance, if I do try to find out.
>
> Anyway, I finally come to my questions. Does anybody have any
> suggestions where one get hold of a computer forensics and/or security
> professional? They would have to have a high enough level of knowledge
> to figure out how the intruder got in, what he/she did on the box,
> given that the usual evidence has been wiped. It might be that the
> intruder still managed to leave some traces, and I hope to find
> someone knowledgeable and experienced enough to discover those traces.
> Also, they would need to be able to figure out if the intruder came in
> from another compromised machine on the lan, and how many boxes on the
> lan have been compromised, whether from the subversion server or
> otherwise. The lan consists of mostly windows machines, and a few
> linux boxes and a few macs. I fear that every machine on the lan has
> been compromised too, either from the subversion box this time, or
> perhaps from last time, or some other way.
>
> If anybody has dealt with forensics people, could they share their
> experiences? Like which professional / firm did a good job and which
> ones to avoid.
>
> I really hope to get some suggestions. The whole thing is a mess and I
> am the guy who knows a lot about security issues around here, which is
> frightening.
>
> If and when we figure out with professional help how the compromise
> happened and what other damage has been done, I'll post the
> information so that others will know what NOT to do.
>
> Looking forward to your replies.

        Once you have installed and configured drupal, you can login

modules can be downloaded and added. All these module management will

hi,

I am getting a fair number of mails from people in Bangalore who want  
to learn/contribute to FOSS, and do not know where to refer them. I  
was wondering whether LUG members in Bangalore could form a Bangalore  
wing of ILUGC - like the Delhi guys have done. All you need to do is  
meet once a month (not on second saturday) so that any enquiries from  
Bangalore could be directed to you. I am sure Mahiti, SpikeSource or  
Yahoo! would be pleased to provide a space for you to meet. Other  
things like availability of resource persons for LDDs and college  
programs, CDs for grabs etc could be put up on a special section of  
the ILUGC website.

Subject: [Ilugc] VLSI FOSS session, Osmania University, December 15, 2007
Message-ID: <d16b1c80712150530v66b8dc52x3e0aaefef2c26d77@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

I was able to get a 30-minute session during the "VLSI-Trends and
Applications" to talk about FOSS VLSI tools, conducted by the
Department of Physics, Osmania University, Hyderabad, today, Saturday,
December 15, 2007. Thanks to Jagan Vemula (Qvantel), and Dr. Lingam
Reddy (Professor, Department of Physics, OU) for their help in this
regard.

I did a short 10-minute presentation (with screenshots):
http://shakthimaan.com/downloads/glv/presentations/vlsi-foss-1.0.odp
http://shakthimaan.com/downloads/glv/presentations/vlsi-foss-1.0.pdf

I then gave them a demo of VHDL examples, and showed them FOSS project
websites (opencores.org, and opencollector.org).
http://www.shakthimaan.com/downloads/glv/embedded-howto/

As usual students didn't ask any questions during the session, but,
had a long offline Q&A and discussion after the session. Some photos:
http://www.shakthimaan.com/Mambo/gallery/album38

Regards,

SK

Shakthi Kannan

From shakthimaan at gmail.com  Sat Dec 15 19:38:13 2007
From: shakthimaan at gmail.com (Shakthi Kannan)
Date: Sat Dec 15 19:38:21 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] TWINCLING.org experience
Message-ID: <d16b1c80712150608y32e550dbu30683e6d05ae84e6@mail.gmail.com>

Hi,

So, I registered for this event http://www.twincling.org/osru, and
didn't get any confirmation e-mail. Some of my friends who registered
late, got an e-mail that they couldn't be alloted because of space
constraints.

But the FAQ said that one can come on the event day, and IT
professionals could pay Rs. 150, and students could pay Rs. 50 and can
join in (now that has been changed in the website).

But, the website still says:

"This is a FREE-of-charge event.

However prior registration at http://www.twincling.org/osru is required. "
http://www.twincling.org/node/180

Being subscribed to the mailing list for few months, technical e-mail
posts to the group doesn't get posted to the group and don't show-up
here:

http://www.mail-archive.com/twincling@yahoogroups.com/

OR here:

http://tech.groups.yahoo.com/group/twincling/

E-mail queries regarding the above to info@twincling.org were not returned.

So, I make a last minute attempt to attend the event, and as quoted in
the website (now that has been changed to registration closed) was
ready to pay Rs. 150 to join in, but, they said 'sorry' and there is
room only for 150 people, and we cannot take in more.

But, the number of registered candidates here is only 140:
http://www.twincling.org/node/188

But, I really, really felt bad for the students who showed up there
(with pens and notebooks) to get some exposure to what was happening
in this FOSS world. I could see the big disappointment in them. I feel
sorry for them, and that I couldn't be of much help to them there.

I returned empty-handed.

SK

-- 
Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

From sundaram at fedoraproject.org  Mon Dec 17 21:59:20 2007
From: sundaram at fedoraproject.org (Rahul Sundaram)
Date: Mon Dec 17 22:07:37 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Alsa upgrade on Fc6
In-Reply-To: <def372aa0712170749w6b007478v210e9dc9c607863c@mail.gmail.com>
References: <def372aa0712170749w6b007478v210e9dc9c607863c@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <4766A3E0.4000807@fedoraproject.org>

ramprasad wrote:
> Hi,
> I have Fc 6 on a HP Pavllion dv 6000. I am able to listen to music on the
> built in speakers.The inbuilt mic doesn't work and when connecting external
> speakers I don't get the sound on the external speakers  thought my built in
> speakers continue to work.
> 
> After searching on the internet, came to know I had to upgrade alsa drivers.
> I downloaded the latest version and alsa-drivers and als-libs and did as
> mentioned in the README. But /proc/asound/version still shows me the old
> version.
> 
> What have I missed ? Do I need to recompile the kernel ?

That wouldn't be required.

# yum install mercurial
# hg clone http://hg.alsa-project.org/alsa-driver alsa-driver
# cd alsa-driver
# ./cvscompile
# make install

Since Fedora Core 6 reached end of life 
(http://fedoraproject.org/wiki/LifeCycle) last week, the best way to get 
updated ALSA drivers is just to upgrade a more recent release of Fedora.

Rahul

References: <7A0ADEC6-22F9-4C2D-B88C-55D8B5BAF464@thenilgiris.com>

2007/12/17, Kenneth Gonsalves <lawgon@thenilgiris.com>:
> hi
> can anyone suggest a good command line tool for conversion of files
> from ogg to mp3?
> --f

fmpeg -i Epoq-Lepidoptera.ogg -vn -ab 64k -ac 1 -ar 22050 -acodec
libmp3lame Epoq-Lepidoptera.mp3

You can use this for all kind of conversions like extracting audio
only from a video also.

Subject: [Ilugc] conversion from ogg to mp3
In-Reply-To: <3f2beab60712172142m486b7d2dse1ce26cd69ceac0c@mail.gmail.com>
References: <7A0ADEC6-22F9-4C2D-B88C-55D8B5BAF464@thenilgiris.com>
	<3f2beab60712172142m486b7d2dse1ce26cd69ceac0c@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20071218073205.GA663@brahma.susmita.org>

On 21:42:02 Dec 17, Praveen A wrote:
> fmpeg -i Epoq-Lepidoptera.ogg -vn -ab 64k -ac 1 -ar 22050 -acodec
> libmp3lame Epoq-Lepidoptera.mp3

I tried and it works too.

$ ffmpeg -i foo.ogg foo.mp3

There is more than one way to skin a cat.

$ sox foo.ogg foo.mp3

$ ogg2mp3 foo.ogg

Multiple pass method.

$ oggdec foo.ogg

$ lame -b 112 foo.wav foo.mp3

There are also other mp3 encoders (excluding ffmpeg) called toolame and
twolame. There is bladeenc but I hear it is not that good.

Of course you can use transcode(1) and mencoder(1) for the same purpose
with the null video input switch.

-Girish

From sundaram at fedoraproject.org  Tue Dec 18 16:50:48 2007
From: sundaram at fedoraproject.org (Rahul Sundaram)
Date: Tue Dec 18 16:59:16 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] conversion from ogg to mp3
In-Reply-To: <7A0ADEC6-22F9-4C2D-B88C-55D8B5BAF464@thenilgiris.com>
References: <7A0ADEC6-22F9-4C2D-B88C-55D8B5BAF464@thenilgiris.com>
Message-ID: <4767AD10.6060907@fedoraproject.org>

Kenneth Gonsalves wrote:
> hi
> can anyone suggest a good command line tool for conversion of files from 
> ogg to mp3?

While there are many tools to do this, this is in general not a good 
idea since you would have a definite loss of quality converting from one 
  lossy format to another.

If you are ripping, rip into lossless formats like FLAC initially and 
then use it for conversion into other lossy formats like Ogg Vorbis for 
general usage.

Rahul

organized, over this weekend.

what
pipesCamp, is an unconference dedicated to yahoo! pipes enthusiasts.  The
one day event would focus on how bloggers, developers as well as
potential end-users could explore yahoo! pipes. There will also be a
contest running through the day for the "Best Pipes" created /
showcased at pipesCamp, with prizes announced at the end of the day.

when
December 23rd, 2007 (Sunday)
10 am - 5 pm IST

where
Chennai , India
( venue information on wiki )

hotel, it would be great to be able to have it iitm/anna univ/
academic location. Do ping me if something can be worked out.

From linuxlingam at gmail.com  Wed Dec 19 00:13:56 2007
From: linuxlingam at gmail.com (Linux Lingam)
Date: Wed Dec 19 00:14:23 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: [urgent] printing from scribus output
Message-ID: <68ddcb070712181043g3bc66e24hf37fbc136549a537@mail.gmail.com>

dear kg and other friends,

have worked extensively with scribus, pdf, and postscript, and spent a
considerable time of my professional years working at pre-press and
press bureau.
so here's how we do this:

author your brochure in scribus.
output as pdf. hyou may choose pdf x-3 as your 'flavour' of pdf.
this flavour of pdf is recommended for pre-press and gets your job out
without hiccups or errors.

even if you don't wish to use pdf x-3, choose the 'pdf for printer'
flavour. it's called 'Output intended for' in the tabbed dialogs of
scribus' pdf output button. you'll probably find it in the 'color'
tab.

beyond this point, the onus lies on your pre-press bureau or printing
plant to get you a proof print from this pdf.
typically, the bureau would have a commercial/professional version of
adobe acrobat, under which a soft-proof of this pdf is checked, and
print-specific technical features like overinking and other issues are
cross-checked.

then, the bureau should provide you with a match-print proof. this may
be a digital printout of this file that closely matches the final
printed brochure. if you okay this, the bureau should go ahead and
offset-print the brochure to deliver you the requested copies.

so if the bureau does not have acrobat professional or does not know
how to handle pdf files, and insists on corel or illustrator or
ventura files?
you've gone to the wrong bureau in 2007.
maybe it is not even a pre-press or repro house.

the migration in the printing industry towards pdf-based workflows
started in 1997. all other forms of workflows preceding pdf-based
workflows have been summarily abandoned long, long ago.
scribus adheres to professional printing standards in its pdf workflows.
please do read my scribus tutorial on the scribus documentation site
or elsewhere, on how to how to handle pdf workflows.

hope this helps.

side-note: before we all jump into a merry discussion around foss and
non-foss software, please do appreciate we're actually talking about
workflows in another industry, namely the printing industry. what they
adopt are professional standards and workflows. if those standards and
workflows are adhered to using foss tools, technologies, and values,
is up to the market forces and policy-decision summits the foss
community can impact. hence fossconf feb 2008 possibly, among several
other initiatives, in our ICT industry.

:-)
niyam bhushan


-- 
niyam bhushan

 On a secondary note, I have used eps output from scribus and
inkscape, to get brocheures printed. Only difference is the printing
is done using digital printing  and not offset.  Depending on the
level of machine handler, you might be presented with silly requests
like "fonts need to be curved" etc. These requests can be handled
easily with respective softwrares.

There must be couple of digital printing press in Chennai too.
As for offset printing, only large printing press have pdf based
workflow. So please check with the printer, if he can handle pdf or
not. From personal experience, almost all printers can handle eps
files, by exporting the eps file to c0rel.

We can do our bit to increase the quantum. My general idea is to
(a) choose a title which broadly fits into the "IEEE" and/or other college
requirements
     and work out a plan for a decent project
(b) guide the students to do at least a partial work -- make it up (using
stubs and drivers) to simulate a full capability. This will be submitted as
the project fulfilling the exam requirements.
(c) coax the students to complete the task -- by themselves or using their
juniors / others.

last year we had an experience with 3 students from Velammal College -- they
completed the full stuff working during May-June (after their final exams.).
>From Stella Maris, two BCA students are taking up their seniors' work.

From girishvenkatachalam at gmail.com  Wed Dec 19 16:46:14 2007
From: girishvenkatachalam at gmail.com (Girish Venkatachalam)
Date: Wed Dec 19 16:46:32 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] how to remove .exe files using tar backup
In-Reply-To: <fb07c0950712190123h41a7a4eeia47f594d8a06a471@mail.gmail.com>
References: <fb07c0950712190123h41a7a4eeia47f594d8a06a471@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20071219111614.GA29341@brahma.susmita.org>

On 14:53:59 Dec 19, ramesh d wrote:
> hi all
> 
> 
> i my smb server some virus is attack it automatcally created *.exe  in each
> and every folder i can,t remove so i first take backup using tar command the
> virus also included how to avoid the *.exe extn file take backup, pls help
> me
> 

First untar it. It can be directly removed from tar as well but this is
more convenient. 

Then type this.

If the directory name is samba/

$ find samba/ -name "*.exe" -type f | xargs rm

But please be careful not to delete system executables.

Ensure this with

$ find samba/ -name "*.exe" -type f -print | less

Best of luck!

Please be careful.

Thanks.

-Girish

>
>Ubuntu 7.10 & Mandriva 2008 x86.
>
>-- 
>Best,
>Z

You can fire up Synaptic in Ubuntu, Select the packages that you need to
install, and then Go to File -> Generate Package download script. 
This creates a script with calls to wget to download all the packages.
Run this on a machine that has internet connectivity and get the
packages locally and install them.

Also, you might want to look at apt-offline or pypt-offline.

From akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in  Wed Dec 19 23:59:42 2007
From: akumar at ee.iitm.ac.in (Kumar Appaiah)
Date: Wed Dec 19 23:52:20 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] build-essential package problem -ubuntu
In-Reply-To: <BAY130-W37056B2E525A9AEC9976DA925C0@phx.gbl>
References: <BAY130-W37056B2E525A9AEC9976DA925C0@phx.gbl>
Message-ID: <20071219182942.GA16669@debian.akumar.iitm.ac.in>

On Wed, Dec 19, 2007 at 11:44:31PM +0530, Dinesh Uthayakumar wrote:
> I had a problem while installing packages.
> it would return
> cc: installation problem, cannot exec `cc1': No such file or directory
> 
> the problem is solved, what i did was
>  cp gcc cc 

This is incorrect. Ubuntu is Debian based, and in these systems, cc
should be symlinkes to a C compiler.

e.g.
[kumar@debian] ls -l /usr/bin/cc
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 20 2005-09-25 20:29 /usr/bin/cc -> /etc/alternatives/cc

> now there are no such errors
> 
> i want explanation !

I really don't know how this happened, but you can (re)install the
build-essential package (or even gcc) to check if the problem
recurs. But copying gcc to cc is not a solution.

Kumar
-- 
Kumar Appaiah,
458, Jamuna Hostel,
Indian Institute of Technology Madras,
Chennai - 600 036

On Thu, Dec 20, 2007 at 12:00:14AM +0530, Dinesh Uthayakumar wrote:
> > I really don't know how this happened, but you can (re)install the
> > build-essential package (or even gcc) to check if the problem
> > recurs. But copying gcc to cc is not a solution.
> 
> Hello Kumar
> 
> Kumar i agree with u and yes i know tat its link !
> but will it lead to any problem ?
> because i tried reinstalling build-essential many times.

Well, you can restore the alternative using update-alternatives. On my
machine, for example:

[kumar@debian ~] sudo update-alternatives --config cc
There is only 1 program which provides cc
(/usr/bin/gcc). Nothing to configure.

So, I just have that:
[kumar@debian ~] ls -l /etc/alternatives/cc
lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 12 2007-12-20 00:16 /etc/alternatives/cc -> /usr/bin/gcc

So, you can try running update-alternatives like I have done, and
choose gcc. Else, manually fix the issue merely by symlinking
/usr/bin/cc to /etc/alternatives/cc and ensure that
/etc/alternatives/cc is symlinked to /usr/bin/gcc.

HTH.

Kumar
-- 
Kumar Appaiah,
458, Jamuna Hostel,
Indian Institute of Technology Madras,
Chennai - 600 036

From: Ivo Emanuel Gon?alves <justivo@gmail.com>
Date: ???? ??????? ?? ??:??
Subject: Re: [Advocate Play Ogg] Help with embedding ogg files in a web page
To: Praveen A <pravi.a@gmail.com>
Cc: advocate@playogg.org


On 12/19/07, Praveen A <pravi.a@gmail.com> wrote:
> Can anyone help here?

There's two ways to embed Ogg Audio AKA Vorbis in a web page:
* the <audio> tag of HTML 5, but it works only in the Firefox and Opera browsers
* the Cortado player, which works everywhere and it's easy to
configure, but computers need to have the Java engine installed (if
the computer uses OpenOffice.org then it has Java support)

Alternative ways are to tell them to use Winamp in Windows, or install
the codecs for Windows Media Player/Quicktime.

The same advice also works for Ogg Video AKA Theora, except instead of
the <audio> tag, one would use the <video> tag.  Windows Media Player
and Quicktime can also work with Ogg Video if the codecs are
installed[1][2].

> If we want to see people using ogg we need to make sure it works everywhere.

This is true, but Mr. Praveen, there's one thing you need to
understand, Ogg is not backed by a big corporation.  Ogg is supported
by the common people like you, and if the common people don't do their
contribution to make sure Ogg works everywhere, then Ogg dies.  The
most important contribution is to publish and share Ogg files on the
Internet and in real life.

-Ivo

[1] http://illiminable.com/ogg/
[2] http://xiph.org/quicktime/

installed Opera.

I don't care what's in HTML 5. It's a non issue if you want to embed media in
web pages until or unless you can expect 90% - not 0.9% like today - of the
people visiting your site to have a browser with support for it.

Everybody, even the guy next door with Win98, have flash installed, and - I
hate to say this - that is what you should be using if you really need to
embed the video in the browser. There are many excellent flash players who
can embed *MP3* files into web pages and that's what you should be doing IF
you want the OGG file embedded in a web page.

If you think it is acceptable to add a "Click here to download" link and add
the text "Then open the file in your favorite ogg/ogm compatible player" then
do use Ogg Vorbis / Theora.

> > * the Cortado player, which works everywhere and it's easy to
> > configure, but computers need to have the Java engine installed (if

Yeah, yeah, Ogg For The Win, etc. But you got to be honest.

You can provide a simple download link to Ogg files and explain how to
obtain/install some players for it. If you really, really need to have audio
embedded into web pages then you can forget Ogg and use a flashplayer which
plays a MP3 file, or forget about it.

Do feel free to correct me if there actually IS a way to put a Ogg file into a
web page which allows 90+% of your visitors to play it. I'd sure as hell like
to know how. And I don't give a crap about oh it's so sad that nobody cares
about Ogg and no corporation supports it and blah blah blah....

The question was "We have someone here trying to embed ogg files in web page
(language lessons) (..) Can anyone help here?" and the answer is NO, you
can't, provide a download link or don't use Ogg.

Praveen A wrote:
> 2007/12/19, Rahul Sundaram <sundaram@fedoraproject.org>:
>> I wasn't aware there is one 'latest and greatest distro'. I am merely
>> reporting the issue. I have no idea what's wrong and it is not my site
>> to debug. It might be even be something to do with the browser and
>> version. I am currently running Mozilla Firefox 2.0.0.10 on Fedora 8. If
>> you need more information, let me know.
>>
> 
> I was able to play these after installing mozilla-mplayer package. It
> is just that (though important) Debian and Fedora did not install
> these browser plugins by default. 

Fedora doesn't include Mplayer in any form in the official repository 
since it is difficult to separate the non-free or patent encumbered 
portions from other portions of Mplayer but third party repositories 
provide those.

In fact Debian had totem-mozilla by
> default and which would have sufficed most users (not in this case for
> sure). I HATE TOTEM. It gets installed by default on every distro and
> it can't play anything (for anything useful with you have install
> totem-xine, and I think debian does that by default) .

This really is a matter of plugins and the media framework. Nowadays 
most players are wrappers around the media frameworks they support. 
Totem supports both gstreamer and Xine framework with distributions 
usually having the gstreamer backend as default. It supports Free 
formats out of the box but you would need additional plugins for other 
formats. With gstreamer, you would need gstreamer-plugins-bad and 
gstreamer-plugins-ugly.

> So install any media-player plugin in Fedora and try.

IIRC totem-mozplugin is installed by default in Fedora but I seem to 
have removed it at some point but Mplayer browser plugin is already 
installed and handles ogg files in other websites but not in Ncrfoss 
one. I tried installing totem plugin as well as the Xine player plugin 
but nothing seems to have resolved this issue.

I have confirmed the same problem in another system running OpenSUSE 
10.3 with Mozilla Firefox 2.0.0.11 with the VLC and Totem browser 
plugins installed FYI.

Rahul

> On Thu, Dec 20, 2007 at 12:00:14AM +0530, Dinesh Uthayakumar wrote:
>>> I really don't know how this happened, but you can (re)install the
>>> build-essential package (or even gcc) to check if the problem
>>> recurs. But copying gcc to cc is not a solution.
>> 
>> Hello Kumar
>> 
>> Kumar i agree with u and yes i know tat its link !
>> but will it lead to any problem ?
>> because i tried reinstalling build-essential many times.
> 
> Well, you can restore the alternative using update-alternatives. On my
> machine, for example:
> 
> [kumar@debian ~] sudo update-alternatives --config cc
> There is only 1 program which provides cc
> (/usr/bin/gcc). Nothing to configure.
> 
> So, I just have that:
> [kumar@debian ~] ls -l /etc/alternatives/cc
> lrwxrwxrwx 1 root root 12 2007-12-20 00:16 /etc/alternatives/cc -> /usr/bin/gcc
> 
> So, you can try running update-alternatives like I have done, and
> choose gcc. Else, manually fix the issue merely by symlinking
> /usr/bin/cc to /etc/alternatives/cc and ensure that
> /etc/alternatives/cc is symlinked to /usr/bin/gcc.
> 
> HTH.
> 
> Kumar

From sbharathi at MidasComm.Com  Fri Dec 21 09:58:20 2007
From: sbharathi at MidasComm.Com (Bharathi Subramanian)
Date: Fri Dec 21 09:59:52 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] [LM] Lua, Lua, Oh, Oh
Message-ID: <Pine.LNX.4.44.0712210954360.1110-100000@bharathi.midascomm.com>

* Lua, Lua, Oh, Oh

Compiled programming languages and scripting languages each have
unique advantages, but what if you could use both to create rich
applications? Lua is an embeddable scripting language that is small,
fast, and very powerful. Before you create yet another configuration
file or resource format (and yet another parser to accompany it), try
Lua.
(http://responses.linux-mag.com/ct.html?rtr=on&s=ax0v,7klu,33o,93ey,dtmo,96lb,6o2h )

* Fighting Performance Regression

Arjan Van De Ven shines some light on the issues, projects, and
techniques that characterize kernel performance.
(http://responses.linux-mag.com/ct.html?rtr=on&s=ax0v,7klu,33o,8o3,kp5x,96lb,6o2h )


* Manageability Technologies in Kernel, User Space, and Beyond

Managing a Linux system can be as easy as connecting to a remote
system and run some of the system tool available with most Linux
distributions. It gets difficult when you have to manage multiple
remote systems, and many Linux admins do work in environments with
hundreds or even thousands of systems.
(http://responses.linux-mag.com/ct.html?rtr=on&s=ax0v,7klu,33o,eeff,m67y,96lb,6o2h )

HTH :)
--
Bharathi S

Who told Hindi is the only national language ?
Have ever read the constitution ?
If possible try to show me(and others in the list) a proof that constitution
tells that  "Hindi is the only National language"

For your info, hindi has only one special status. It was proposed to replace
english with hindi as "official and communication language" for Indian Govt.

But that proposal was dropped later after protests from states like Tamil
Nadu.  English usage as official language of india continues and hindi also
is used as official language in hindi speaking states.
thats all..
other than the above there is no special status to hindi over other
"National languages of India" like tamil, malayalam, telugu, bengali etc...

May be you can read the following links:
http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Official_languages_of_India
http://www.constitution.org/cons/india/const.html (can read online here)
http://india.gov.in/govt/constitutions_india.php ( you can download pdf
formats)

Praveen A wrote:
> 2007/12/21, Rahul Sundaram 

>>> Is mplayer and mplayer plugin installed by default in Mandriva?
>> Probably does or atleast would be in the repository. They don't have to
>> worry about U.S Patents being a French company.
> 
> Debian faced this same problem and it solved it only recently. I think
> Fedora can use debian's version (stripped with no known patent
> encumbered bits) if they want to. It took more than 7 years to enter
> debian and that too after mplayer did an audit of their code for any
> patent infringements.

Debian is more concerned about copyright and what they did as well as 
what was done within the Mplayer development team was primary a 
copyright license audit and not a patent audit. Refer

http://people.debian.org/~mjr/legal/mplayer.html

If you are a non-profit, a patent holder can merely ask you to stop 
distribution until the patent issues are resolved but otherwise a claim 
of monetary damages can be made which may run into millions of dollars.

Debian being a legally established non-profit via SPI has ignored 
potential patent issues several times in the past and they even ship a 
MP3 decoder in their base distribution. While the Debian work is useful 
as regards to copyright licenses, their work cannot be treated as 
authoritative when it comes to patents.

> That was the time when totem was not using any of these frame work
> (anyone ubuntu 4.10 - was that the first version? or was it 5.10?)

Totem has been using both these frameworks for a very long time and even 
before Ubuntu ever existed.

> Any sites that use embed tag? 

Not sure. If you have any websites that embed ogg video and does not use 
java applets, let me know and I will check that.

Rahul
From girishvenkatachalam at gmail.com  Sat Dec 22 07:34:07 2007
From: girishvenkatachalam at gmail.com (Girish Venkatachalam)
Date: Sat Dec 22 07:34:32 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] lua script to download youtube videos
Message-ID: <20071222020407.GA24669@brahma.susmita.org>

First of all this script was written by erstwhile OpenBSD developer
Pedro Martelleto.

You might have to take care of dependencies. It does an amazing job.

Take a look at the power of lua.

I love lua but I know nothing about it. ;)

Play with it and enjoy. 

-Girish


#!/usr/local/bin/lua
-- $OpenBSD: yt.lua,v 1.7 2007/11/09 00:26:29 jolan Exp $
-- Fetch videos from YouTube.com and convert them to MPEG.
-- Written by Pedro Martelletto in August 2006. Public domain.
-- Example: lua yt.lua http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=c5uoo1Kl_uA

http = require("socket.http")

-- Make sure a URL was given.
url = assert(arg[1], "Wrong usage, no URL given")

-- Set this to a command capable of talking HTTP and following 3XX requests.
fetch = "ftp -o <file> <url>"

-- Set this to a command capable of converting from FLV to MPEG.
convert = "ffmpeg -y -i <flv> -b 1000k -f mp4 -vcodec mpeg4 -acodec libfaac -ab 128k <mp4> 1>/dev/null 2>&1"

-- Set this to the base location where to fetch YouTube videos from.
base_url = "http://www.youtube.com/get_video?video_id="

-- Fetch the page holding the embedded video.
print(string.format("Getting %s ...", url))
body = assert(http.request(url))

-- Look for the video title.
pattern = "<meta name=\"title\" content=\"(.-)\""
title = assert(string.match(body, pattern))

-- Build a name for the files the video will be stored in.
file = string.gsub(title, " ", "_")
file = string.gsub(title, "[^%w-]", "_")
file = "youtube-" .. string.lower(file)
flv = file .. ".flv"
mp4 = file .. ".mp4"

-- Escape the file names.
e_flv = string.format("%q", flv)
e_mp4 = string.format("%q", mp4)

-- Look for the video ID.
pattern = "/watch_fullscreen.*video_id=(.-)&fs="
id = assert(string.match(body, pattern))

-- Fetch the video.
url = string.format("%q", base_url .. id)
cmd = string.gsub(fetch, "<(%w+)>", { url = url, file = e_flv })
assert(os.execute(cmd) == 0, "Failed")

-- Convert it to MPEG.
cmd = string.gsub(convert, "<(%w+)>", { flv = e_flv, mp4 = e_mp4 })
print("Converting ...")
assert(os.execute(cmd) == 0, "Failed")

os.remove(flv)
print("Done. Video saved in " .. mp4 .. ".")

From technocraze at gmail.com  Sat Dec 22 20:56:17 2007
From: technocraze at gmail.com (senthilraja P)
Date: Sat Dec 22 20:56:27 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Re: Re: Bangalorians from ILUGC (???????????)
In-Reply-To: <407676.64264.qm@web33305.mail.mud.yahoo.com>

	<407676.64264.qm@web33305.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <c9ea6e770712220726w8948a53v58e923d24aab0dcb@mail.gmail.com>

I agree with Ramdass here..  How can we bring our language to computers, if
we ourselves are not ready to use it?

The important practical point here is that, if we strive to localise
computers, then we should be the first one, who should use it in our
languages.

And for the sake of localisation, we need not neglect english too.  The
point is that one should learn both english and our mother tongue, and
should be trained to use computers in both.

To quote an example, we have seen lot of websites in dutch, or french or
german languages..  Some of the mailing lists are too in such languages.  It
doesnt mean that they dont know english.  But they prefer to use the
language which they would understood firsthand, rather than to use english
and them translate and understand.

My points are:

1. We should strive to use corresponding language in local mailing list. (In
chennai lug, tamil)
2. We should strive to use Hindi for National Communication.
3. In case Hindi is not familiar, then we can use english.

This is unthinkable as of now, because, none of us are trained to read mails
in tamil..  But, if at all we want to bring about dignity, indigneous, and
to bring our mother tongu in computers, we should be ready to bring them in
to our daily life.  and this does not necessary be at the cost of english..

There would be lot of problems initially, but if more people are committed
then it will become used to us.

Regards,
Senthil

There is a small part of readers who cannot read Tamil
here. Almost all users here are comfortable with
English as a medium of communication. The purpose of
having a mailing list like this(in my opinion) is to
share your knowledge and reply to topics of your
interest. Once the medium of communication changes to
anything other than English, we have no clue of whats
going on here.
    Most people come here to get educated and help
others with free/open source software. I just don't
see how learning linux in English is any less
dignified than learning it in any of the Indian
languages. As far as it appears, one should go with
the language most of the readers can follow.
    Dignity is in sharing your knowledge in a medium
that can be followed by majority of the readers. 



From: senthilraja P <technocraze@...>

To quote an example, we have seen lot of websites in
dutch, or french or
german languages..  Some of the mailing lists are too
in such languages.  It
doesnt mean that they dont know english.  But they
prefer to use the
language which they would understood firsthand, rather
than to use english
and them translate and understand.

My points are:

1. We should strive to use corresponding language in
local mailing list. (In
chennai lug, tamil)
2. We should strive to use Hindi for National
Communication.
3. In case Hindi is not familiar, then we can use
english.

This is unthinkable as of now, because, none of us are
trained to read mails
in tamil..  But, if at all we want to bring about
dignity, indigneous, and
to bring our mother tongu in computers, we should be
ready to bring them in
to our daily life.  and this does not necessary be at
the cost of english..

There would be lot of problems initially, but if more
people are committed
then it will become used to us.

From mohan34u at gmail.com  Sun Dec 23 12:16:36 2007
From: mohan34u at gmail.com (Mohan R)
Date: Sun Dec 23 12:16:49 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Network driver detection failure
In-Reply-To: <0E21E0A9-F89D-4863-9378-210EEE727415@thenilgiris.com>
References: <27d8eda00712221034w25ac579drfca325c3c2263719@mail.gmail.com>
	<0E21E0A9-F89D-4863-9378-210EEE727415@thenilgiris.com>
Message-ID: <4262d4520712222246k1fb0fdf6s630ce0f6d93131e4@mail.gmail.com>

What kind of problem u faced? Is that the ethernet card is detected? try
with 'dmesg | grep "eth0" ' then see whether kernel detects your ethernet or
not.

I had a problem when configuring network. But for me, the card is detected
but dhcpcd failed to configure my network. I use the above command to
confirm ethernet card detected.

then I tried the below commands

ifconfig eth0 down
rmmod 8139too
modprobe 8139too media=0x01
ifconfig eth0 up
dhcpcd

thats all my network configured. My card is RTL 8139(Real Talk).

From m.sujith at gmail.com  Sun Dec 23 13:09:19 2007
From: m.sujith at gmail.com (Sujith)
Date: Sun Dec 23 13:11:37 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Network driver detection failure
In-Reply-To: <27d8eda00712221034w25ac579drfca325c3c2263719@mail.gmail.com>
References: <27d8eda00712221034w25ac579drfca325c3c2263719@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <476E10A7.5010803@gmail.com>

PV Sundarram wrote:
> Hi luggers,
> I am trying to install etch on a system with asus p5gc-mx motherboard which
> has a inbuilt network card.
> In the installation phase, it is not detecting the network card.
> 
> Has any one faced a similar problem and solved the issue?

P5GC-MX has an Attansic Ethernet chipset.
Driver support for Attansic based boards were added recently to the 
linux kernel,
and is now part of the mainline tree under the name atl1.
Debian Etch has an older kernel ( 2.6.18 ? ) which I think doesn't 
include atl1.
You can either manually upgrade the kernel or try compiling the vendor 
provided driver.
The vendor driver can be obtained from : 
ftp://hogchain.net/pub/linux/attansic/vendor_driver/
The choice is up to you.

Sujith
-- 
http://m.sujith.googlepages.com
