List,

FreeIndian is all about introducing Indian FOSS contributors to the 
world. Individuals listed here contribute to various Free and Open 
Source projects. They include programmers, artists, translators, FOSS 
advocates, maintainers, packagers and many other direct or indirect 
FOSS contributors. Read on to know what Indian FOSS developers are all 
about, how they entered the realm of FOSS, how much time they spend on 
it, what are their opinions about FOSS, and what are their likes and 
dislikes.

FreeIndian is based loosely on the format of BehindKDE, which features 
KDE developers across the world.

Our current interviews features one more [http://code.google.com/soc 
Google Summer of Code GSoC] candidate who got involved in PHP 
initially, learned it alongside his course at Jaipur. He's a native 
Chennai-aite, born in Delhi and is pursuing his education in Jaipur. 
Read the interview, to know more about Gentoo user, here.

http://kde.in/index.php/Anant_Narayan

You can use compix fusion with the fglrx driver.
It might take a little tinkering with xorg.conf to get things running 
smoothly.
And AIGLX is unsupported, though I believe it has been added in the 
recent catalyst drivers.

Or, if you are willing to take the plunge, you can give the experimental 
driver 'radeonhd' a try.
radeonhd is the new open source driver that is in development.

And, why are you forced to use Windows ? :)

Subject: [Ilugc] [JOB] Intern with Python skills & Web designer
Message-ID: <476F42B5.50508@gmail.com>

Hi,

We are Viamentis Technologies, a small web development company based out 
of Chennai. We provide cutting-edge product development services for 
several web 2.0 startups across the world (mostly using Ruby on Rails).

Recently we got an unusual request from one of our local clients - she 
wanted us to modify a fairly popular open source python learning tool 
for their internal use. The changes seem to be extensive, so there is a 
good chance that some of the work can be contributed back to the project.

Since we don't have any Pythonistas among our colleagues, we thought 
inviting a final year student over and offering him a project would be a 
good idea to learn it along with him/her. We also pay a small stipend to 
students who are working with us.

So if you are a student looking for a real-world final year project, 
which will be important to the client's day-to-day work, drop us a line. 
If the client is happy with your work, apart from getting a certificate 
of completion from us, we will also arrange for a letter of appreciation 
from the client. I don't know how useful it is going to be, but I hope 
it helps :).

What are we looking for? Self-starters, who have good Python knowledge, 
who are passionate about technology and can learn new things on their 
own. What do you get in return? A caring and encouraging work 
environment that always challenges you to do better, and respects your 
individuality (seriously, we allow shorts in our office).

You will get the same treatment we give to our full-timers. And probably 
help convert a few Rubyists into the Python camp. Write to us at: intern 
at viamentis d0t com. What's more, if you really shake things up here, 
there maybe a job offer waiting for you at the end of the project.

Next, we are looking for a web designer to work with us on a an 
consultant/hourly basis - you should be able to talk & walk the web 2.0 
design lingo well - rounded corners, drop shadows, css sprites, XHTML, 
css, etc. If you're good, we pay well. If you're really good, there 
might be a job offer waiting you at the end of the assignment. Please 
write us at: webdesigner at viamentis d0t com. (If you can also point to 
your work online or attach some of your previous work, it would be 
great). If you're a fresher to web design but you think you have some 
talent and willing to learn fast, show us your work, we could talk.


Thanks much,
Vamsee Kanakala
Viamentis Technologies Pvt. Ltd.

This is a major issue here..  That's why i said, we will face lot of
challenges initially..

Probably,  those who dont know tamil in chennai LUG, can put effort to learn
it, and participate in discussion..

But anything should not be forced..  If there is no unanimous decision, its
better to put it off.

Please remember, this is not about dignity or something else.  Let's look it
as an opportunity to bring our mother tongue in to practice.

My personal opinion is that we cannot bring about change JUST by learning..
instead, we have to put in to practice what we want to bring about.

Instead of getting "Can or Cannot", let's just look in to feasibities of
this option.. If its not feasible as of now, let's wait for some more time
till a consensus is reached.

My practical solutions:

1. Those who are in ILUG-Chennai, but dont know tamil, can strive to learn
it.  After all, its one of the languages of our country.. (if we are willing
to learn french/german etc for money, there's no reason why we should not
learn our own languages.

2. If any one is in Calcutta, and part of Calcutta mailing list, let him
learn Bengali..  and let other members help him on that.


Where there is a will, there is a way.. :)

REgards,
senthil

senthilraja P wrote:
> My practical solutions:
>
> 1. Those who are in ILUG-Chennai, but dont know tamil, can strive to learn
> it.  After all, its one of the languages of our country.. (if we are willing
> to learn french/german etc for money, there's no reason why we should not
> learn our own languages.
>

Ok, this is really getting tiresome. First of all, the discussion is no 
longer related to its' title. And this is such a tired old topic that I 
don't even read fully when I see something like "we should use Tamil/why 
use Tamil". Bang, delete. But sometimes, just sometimes, it just gets to 
you.

<rant on>I'm all for learning Tamil - coming from a different part of 
the country, I really make an effort to learn the language. I feel proud 
when somebody compliments that I'm picking it up fast. But I get put off 
when somebody else suggests that I "should" do so, there is no harm in 
learning the language of the land, blah blah. Especially so, in a 
technical forum.

I come here to gain or if possible spread knowledge about Linux/Foss, 
not get lectured about learning a regional language. Whether I learn a 
language or not is my own business. I learn it when I think it is an 
advantage to do so. Otherwise, I won't. So everybody stop tooting their 
horns about their love for regional language, everybody loves their own 
mother tongue/regional language, and nobody is doing any other person a 
favor picking up a particular language. If it is useful, they will pick 
it up. Otherwise, not.

I fail to understand the logic of suggesting people learn the language, 
because I am always considerate enough to talk in English even if there 
is one colleague that doesn't understand our conversation, even if there 
are 10 others who do. It seems like such a minimal civility. If you are 
sadistic/bigoted enough to write in a script that you know some people 
won't understand, please do so. We will roll our eyes and continue to 
ignore the mails. But don't tell me to learn it, because you have no 
business doing so.</rant off>

There. I feel better now.

V.

 was Tamil.

        I have no idea what the numbers might look like, or what the
 relative benefits to the membership would be like; but most of the
 discussion I have seen seems to not have delved into the issue of the
 impact of the decision.  For instance, the statement above that those
 who do not know Language A can just learn it might not be a viable
 solution to many people (and yes, that is true for people saying that
 respondents should just learn English as well.)

        While I read this mailing list, I am not anywhere close to
 Chennai -- I live in the US, and I merely monitor this list in case
 there are questions people have about Debian/free software that I could
 help with. Learning Tamil in Tennessee is harder than you would think
 (and my inclination would be to go with Spanish, Greek, or Sanskrit
 first, given the utility that the learning would bring me given where I
 live).

From girishvenkatachalam at gmail.com  Tue Dec 25 07:57:53 2007
From: girishvenkatachalam at gmail.com (Girish Venkatachalam)
Date: Tue Dec 25 07:58:13 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] [OT]Generating traffic on blog
In-Reply-To: <406f1f3f0712241301h18332a93v56f35234c1b8700f@mail.gmail.com>
References: <406f1f3f0712241301h18332a93v56f35234c1b8700f@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <20071225022753.GA5554@brahma.susmita.org>

On 02:31:07 Dec 25, Anoop John wrote:
> Hi,
> I have been writing this blog http://thondomraughts.blogspot.com for
> quite some time and have around 35 posts on the site. I have not been
> able to generate any traffic on the blog - neither organic nor
> otherwise. I have read through a lot of SEO stuff but nothing seems to
> be working. Can anybody point me to some good tips or give me some
> good tips that can start giving some immediate results.

Your mail is quite frank and sincere.

There are some really successful people in this respect in LUG. There is
Shrinivasan T who is running http://fossjobs.wordpress.com. He says he
gets very impressive hit statistics there. His
http://goinggnu.wordpress.com site is doing very well too.

I have no experience creating or running popular websites but I would
guess the general principles of life apply. The cyber world is just a
projection of real world. 

The key idea can be summed up in two sentences.

"Help others so others help you and come to you for help. Building
goodwill is the basis of all success."

Another thing you need to know about economics on the Internet. The
typical MBA attitude of money, money, money will not work.

Unless you give knowledge, software, artwork whatever; your labor of
love for free, your site will never be popular. Internet economy is by
nature a free economy. One person cannot change it.

If you have content on your blog that others benefit by visiting your
site, automatically with time your site will become popular. google will
pick it up and you will start making ad revenue(in case you are
interested in this).

You should also wait patiently for the most effective marketing strategy
on earth - "the word of mouth" propagation to take place.

"Word of mouth" advertising incidentally has a mathematical model too.
It works remarkably well since it has an exponential growth pattern.

For those of you who are hearing 'word of mouth' for the first time,
suffice it to say that it is the sort of
marketing/advertising/canvassing in which the customers speak for you
based on their experience. This is far better than you going around and
telling people that your product/service is good.

You can also do your mite by spreading the word amongst your contacts.

I would imagine that any worthy useful endeavor in life takes a few
years at least.

So you should be patient and keep applying your shoulder to the wheel.

I read somewhere recently that to become a really good C programmer it
takes more than 7 years and that too if you are within the top 15% of
intelligence.

This is why I feel like laughing whenever students and other kids (
people who are just 1 or 2 years into the industry) say.

" Oh C? It is easy man. I know that language well."

As usual I have digressed. Hope you get the idea.

Best of luck!

-Girish

People who have been subscribed to this list for more than a couple of years
have learnt to grit our teeth and ignore discussions on this topic - which
keeps recurring every few months!

The fears expressed the first time - that the list will soon be flooded with
posts in 14 languages and that the noise will drown out the signal - did not
turn out to be real. In fact, even Tamil posts are few in number. It was
decided earlier that posts in tamil /other lang would be tagged as such
making it easier to configure your filters.

So, why don't we quit this pointless discussion and keep moving!! If it
comes to a point that the vernacular posts so outnumber the english ones
then perhaps we can have a vote and impose some restrictions. Till then,
live and let live. I guess we all are fighting for a free world, right?

regds,
mano

--- srini vasan wrote:

> Hello,Now i am downloading Ubunthu 7.00. Ubunthu
> 7.00 is downloading file name is
> ubunthu-7.10-desktop.i386.iso

Correction, the file would be name
ubuntu-7.10-desktop.i386.iso

> How can i install
> ubunthu using this file.Whether i want to copy this
> iso file to cd.How can i install after downloading
> this file.

It may not be easier to install using iso file, though
possible. I assume, you are currently using Windows
and have downloaded the ISO file.

Assuming that there are no errors (or none occurred
during downloading the ISO) in the ISO, you can burn
the ISO using Nero in Windows. There's a menu Copy CD/
DVD within nero, which lists "Burn ISO to disc". 

Select that option that'll open a file dialog enabling
you to select the ISO file. (Preferably, use a CD-RW
disc) 

The entire installation procedure cannot be covered
within a single email, therefore, I would request you
to refer to 

http://help.ubuntu.com/


>Please help
> me.

HTH.

Note, installation of the OS, is assumed to be a very
easy task these days, and therefore, you /may/ not
find many replying to your posts. 

Consequently, one (or you) are expected to read guides
at http://wiki.ubuntu.com to get started.

Ahoy! I got this idea just a few minutes ago and immediately
registered it as a talk. We have been having (GPG/PGP) Key Signing
Party in almost every FOSS conference, why not have one in ours. Thus,
there will be a brief session on creating GPG Keys, followed by a Key
Signing Party during fossconf chennai feb08.

What you need to do? Generate your own GPG keys[1], print the finger
print on strips of paper (you can bring your own hand written ones
too), bring it along with an ID Proof. You can also upload it to
Biglumber [2] Lets share them and sign each other's keys. :)

[1] http://www.doc.ic.ac.uk/csg/faqs/gpghowto.html
[2] http://biglumber.com/x/web?ak=1

Subject: [Ilugc] Using Microsoft Anti-Piracy Raids to promote Linux
In-Reply-To: <406f1f3f0712251234p45387dd7kfb9d7ba29c74ea81@mail.gmail.com>
References: <406f1f3f0712251234p45387dd7kfb9d7ba29c74ea81@mail.gmail.com>
Message-ID: <527acce10712252337r6577ea39l87bda22a14f8d613@mail.gmail.com>

I always believe that anti-piracy raids will help to promote linux usage.
Government doesn't need to promote Linux or opensource, they just need to
find strict ways to stop piracy(like raids). I think in India, BSA is
responsible for conducting these raids. It is nice to hear even M$ is doing
for their products. These raids can help in both ways, either the
user/organisation will go and buy legal software or they will find better
solutions in FOSS.

Can anybody explain why these raids are always targetted against small
shops/organization/training centres? Why it is not done against individuals?
I know it is impossible to do that. What can be done to stop this at
individual level? My assumption is piracy spreads mostly through custom
hardware assemblers. It is less through other ways.

Finally why can't there be a law to enforce every organisation to get
inspected(every year) for using illegal software? Is it too costly affair
todo raids. The fund to implement this can be generated through government,
BSA and from the fines imposed on the notorious companies.

-- Guru Prasath

Hi all,

How about including the following  in the list guidelines?

"The lingua franca of this list is English and will remain English. However,
since this is a bastion of freedom, no language will be discriminated
against - as long as the post is tagged appropriately. Example, for Tamil it
shall be [TAMIL] (not [TAMIZH] pls) and for Hindi it will be [HINDI]. And
for Swahili, Nyanja and Tonga it shall be [SWAHILI], [NYANJA] and [TONGA]
respectively. Thank you very much.

While thats the official position, if you are serious about getting a
response to your query please stick to English! There are just not enough
members here who will be able to understand and respond to your query in the
language of your choice."

If its OK, request this to be included in the mailing list guidelines. The
next time a language war crops up we can point the warring parties to this

From prem at songbirdtech.com  Wed Dec 26 19:04:19 2007
From: prem at songbirdtech.com (Prem Kurian Philip)
Date: Wed Dec 26 19:04:28 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Using Microsoft Anti-Piracy Raids to promote Linux
Message-ID: <44815.61.247.255.57.1198676059.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>

>Can anybody explain why these raids are always targetted against small
>shops/organization/training centres? Why it is not done against individuals?
>I know it is impossible to do that. What can be done to stop this at
>individual level? My assumption is piracy spreads mostly through custom
>hardware assemblers. It is less through other ways.

Two reasons:

1) Organizations can pirate much more than any single individual.

2) It costs money to conduct a raid. If there is not enough pay out (fines
or software licenses), then it doesn't make sense to conduct a raid.
Raiding individuals is too expensive and is not a good use of the
resources of the BSA or companies such as MS.  When MS or BSA conduct
raids, they will allow the organization to purchase licenses (and also pay
a fine). How many licenses would an individual want to purchase? From the
point of maximum bang for the buck, it makes sense to raid organizations
and not individuals.

Regards,
PK

 think blogging gives them influence, then there is bound to be
 disappointment; since very few of the top ever achieve either goal.

        Like free software, blogs are best if you are blogging to
 scratch your own itch; because then the  the satisfaction in your own
 work does not depend on external factors; but within yourself.  I think
 I have just re-phrased the Bhagawata Geeta for the modern age :-)

        manoj
--

From anoopjohn at gmail.com  Thu Dec 27 02:59:41 2007
From: anoopjohn at gmail.com (Anoop John)
Date: Thu Dec 27 02:59:50 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] Using Microsoft Anti-Piracy Raids to promote Linux
In-Reply-To: <44815.61.247.255.57.1198676059.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>
References: <44815.61.247.255.57.1198676059.squirrel@www.songbirdtech.com>
Message-ID: <406f1f3f0712261329i64b5b06crdce4cbb1c35f469@mail.gmail.com>

Although I agree theoretically with what is said on simplymalayalees
forum, I have reservations about the way the argument is put forward.
I run a software company and I agree that people will have to pay for
the work done in creating the software. In a normal market when the
traded volume of a given product goes up the cost of the product has
to come down. It has not happened with windows. The cost has been
recovered several times over. What we see here is the effects of the
Monopoly Microsoft is enjoying in the market. Again my opinion is not
to legally fight the monopoly or to deny microsoft to make the profit
but rather, concerned people should take necessary steps to invigorate
the market by introducing alternative options. That is precisely what
the Linux community is doing.
Here is a more detailed discussion on the above issue
<http://thondomraughts.blogspot.com/2007/12/piracy-is-not-fair-neither-is-monopoly.html>
Cheers
Anoop

On Dec 26, 2007 6:25 PM, senthilraja P <technocraze@gmail.com> wrote:
> My suggestion is to never care for visitors.  Just let's concentrate on
> putting contents that are really worth.  It may click any time.
>

We have got an internal blogging system in my company (hosted on
FLOSS). I was talking to some of the most *popular* bloggers.
According to them, you get more visitors if you already have visitors
commenting on your blogs. To get more people commenting on your blog,
you have to comment on others blogs.

To generate more traffic on your own blog, visit other's blogs
frequently and keep commenting on theirs. They would return in kind.
Most of the people who read blogs would either be having their own
blogs or would be following their friend's (or some one special's)
blogs. So, if they find your name in their blogs, it generates more
traffic.

Cheers,
Natarajan

Hi,

----- On Dec 27, 2007 2:09 PM, ThangarajanG <thangamu@gmail.com> wrote:
|  My modem Out put has 192.168.1.xxx range. My router (Netgear) has
192.168.0.xxx range ...
|  My access point is in Router range and I have changed the ip
address to 192.168.0.240.
\--

Note:
- Wired connection
~ Wireless connection

This is how I would debug.

Setup I:
Modem<--1->Router<-2-->PC

Make sure connection 1 and 2 are fine with ping. You should also check
that you can browse the Internet from PC.

Setup II:
Access Point <--3--> PC

Test ping for connection 3, and make sure it is ok.

Setup III:
Modem<--1->Router<~~2~~>Access point
                        4|
                        PC

Test ping from PC to access point. If it fails, check ping between
router and access point.

Setup IV:
Modem<--1->Router<~~2~~>Access point<--3--> PC

Test ping between PC to router.

Maybe others have other suggestions.

SK

Shakthi Kannan
http://www.shakthimaan.com

I was searching for anti-piracy raids and came across this page

http://members.microsoft.com/partner/india/IPRCase1.aspx

"A recent BSA-IDC study points out the impact of reduction in piracy
in India. It states that a reduction from the 70% level in 2002 to 60%
by 2006 will add $2 billion to India's economy, increase local
industry revenues by around $1.6 billion, generate 48,435 new
high-tech, high-wage jobs and generate $92.4 million in tax revenues
for the government. The projected IT growth during 2002-06 will stand
at 148% if the piracy rate continues at the present level of 70%.
However, the 10-percentage point reduction can up that growth to
163%."

Funny how they came up with the exact number of IT jobs :).
Also interesting the way they have estimated IT growth if piracy is reduced.
I wonder how by increasing a company's expenses it is going to grow faster.
The tax of 92 Million Dollar seems to be too low for the sales
required to match the above data. A brief analysis of the data is
given as a comment at

>> And, why are you forced to use Windows ? :)
> For running Google Earth and other 3D apps.

> Btb. does the Open source radeon driver support 3D and H/w Acceleration.

As of now, 3D support is lacking in the radeonhd driver.
I tried using a git build of radeonhd and it was pretty primitive.
A lot of artifacts all over the place, no XVideo suppport and was 
virtually unusable.

Fglrx is your best choice for now - it has a decent feature set and is 
quite stable.
The most recent version of catalyst - 7.12-2 has a lot of regressions.
It doesn't detect the resolutions properly and I had to revert to an 
earlier version.

I have not had much experience with compiz fuzion / XGL.
Am biased towards a more minimalist desktop, without any bling. :)

From rajsekhar.kvs at gmail.com  Thu Dec 27 22:36:26 2007
From: rajsekhar.kvs at gmail.com (rajasekhar kuppa)
Date: Thu Dec 27 22:36:39 2007
Subject: [Ilugc] help require in converting my server to NAS box
In-Reply-To: <546457.2618.qm@web31906.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
References: <546457.2618.qm@web31906.mail.mud.yahoo.com>
Message-ID: <446cb7260712270906wbb5aaferae1e5578df80502d@mail.gmail.com>

>
> In my work place we don't have any NAS box. we are
> having one dell server model "SC430" it is a intel
> pentium with dual core processor.
>
> I would like to convert the server to a NAS box. I
> tried in the google search and found one freenas. I
> don't know wheather it will stable one.
>


There are two ways in which you can acheive this.

1) Run an operating system (GNU/ Linux or BSD  or something else)  and then
run samba or NFS on top of it as is your requirement.  This will have a very
low  knowledge curve( provided you are already good with administration. But
the down side is that there will be too many unnecessary services running
and it will not be scalable.

2) The other way is to run dedicated footprint OS like FreeNAS  or Open
Filer.
These require a good deal of attention from you and the knowledge curve is
very high. But the dividends will pay off in the long run. IF you want
scalability then Open filer  can eventually even be used not just as  a NAS
option but can be scaled up as a SAN ( IPSAN albeit) with iscsi  as the
underlying protocol.

and if you need professional support at  some point the open filer team also
sells some commercial support.

so it all depends on how big a hammer do you want :-)
if all you need is just  an interdepartmental file server for some 50 to 100
pcs. well just insttall samba and be done with it.

Reggies
Raj

From girishvenkatachalam at gmail.com  Fri Dec 28 12:29:23 2007

On 10:31:04 Dec 28, Padhu Indianathann wrote:
> Dear experts,
>                 I want following commands
> 1. The command to list out total files briefly in the folder, number of
> files in the folder and also to display the size of folder.
>      For example /root/asd folder
>      # ls-l; ls -l | grep wc -l
>    The above command display the files into asd and number of files also.
> but how to get the total size of folder
> 2. I wish  to view the content and size of *.tar.gz and *.tar.bz file with
> its size

Your questions are not very clear to me.

There are no bz files, only bz2 files and you can list the contents with 

$ tar jtf *.tar.bz2 | less

You should use a combination of ls, find and du with the right flags.

Some tips.

  a) ls -a will display hidden files
  b) ls -lR will recursively list all files
  c) du -hsc * will display useful stuff, check it out ;)
  d) ls -l | grep -v ^d will display only files excluding dirs 
  e) find . -type f -print will recursively print all files

You could also use locate(1) in case the locate.db(5) is current.

Best bet would be to run updatedb as root manually.

Hope this helps.

-Girish

On 01:20:14 Dec 29, Nisha Mary wrote:
> I want to work with RTLinux and in open source. Can i get a chance. Anyone
> help me. I have completed embedded course and trained in RTLinux

You can download rtlinux and compile it and get started.

But if you are new to linux and having just finished an education in rtlinux
I would think that you might get a little frustrated/uncomfortable
working in the linux environment. Don't worry. It is the same way even
with experts. It is always hard in the beginning.

A good idea might be to try out Ubuntu liveCD distributions or one of
the numerous other "friendly" linux distros. Once you are familiar with
the environment and shell commands you can move on to hacking rtlinux.

Best of luck!

Should you have any questions you can always post to this list and
people will help. Please ask descriptive questions after doing a
thorough research and reading the documentation.

Thanks.

-Girish

Shakthi Kannan wrote:
> Check the network driver specification or data sheet? or ask the
> vendor? For example, for Intel e1000 gigabit ethernet (check Jumbo
> frames):
> http://downloadmirror.intel.com/13811/ENG/e1000.htm
Jumbo frames are supported by very few drivers. Also, as one does not 
live in isolation, it is better to go with std MTU. Even if your laptop 
supports Jumbo frames, it is very likely that downstream equipment drops 
Jumbo frames. Gets you nowhere then.

Question is why does one need Jumbo frames for normal apps? If not, 
better to stick with what works.

Mohan

> the environment and shell commands you can move on to hacking rtlinux.

A request to members. Can you refrain from replying to digest mails 
please? It screws up the context for threaded email reading and folks 
rarely resort to pruning of the mail to relevant contents for which 
reply is being sent.

The case in hand is a reply by Sanjeev Saini on RTLinux help.

First let me wish you a happy new year. This is to let you know that

for supporting Linux in and around Trivandrum. We currently have the
mailing list ilug-tvm@googlegroups.com. I believe there must be a few
people from Trivandrum in ilug-c. If so please do come join the fun at
http://groups.google.com/group/ilug-tvm.

On 20:10:43 Dec 31, Mohan Sundaram wrote:
> A request to members. Can you refrain from replying to digest mails please? 
> It screws up the context for threaded email reading and folks rarely resort 
> to pruning of the mail to relevant contents for which reply is being sent.
>
> The case in hand is a reply by Sanjeev Saini on RTLinux help.
>

Though I appreciate the spirit and purpose of this mail I believe we
should be far far more forgiving.

After all this is a newbie/beginners list and we should definitely make
room for others to participate.

One of the reasons many great people left LUG  never to return is due to
the occasionally unfriendly attitude sometimes seen. It is only one of
the reasons. And I am only guessing. I could well be wrong. 

I am still wondering why they left. But we can at least create new great
people...

I am definitely not pointing my finger at anybody as I never ever want
to do that.

This is just an observation in the light of the fact that the activity
is a lot less nowadays and also the technical depth of discussions are
appallingly low. I can scarcely believe that this is the same list that
taught me LaTeX, difference between NAS and SAN and recently about jumbo
frames. (And helped me build countless other contacts which are too
numerous for me to enumerate)

It is impossible to make any endeavor succeed without the right people
and the only way to attract the right people is by a friendly attitude.
And a progressive culture of meritocracy and excellence.

We never know who is going to become a useful technical help in future.

I was a clueless beginner newbie in the OpenBSD lists two years ago. Nobody found fault with me...

Have a great 2008!

-Girish
